</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a>
</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Shanghai" title="Port of Shanghai">Port of Shanghai</a>
</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Bridge" title="San Francisco Bay Bridge">San Francisco Bay Bridge</a>

</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a>

</li></ul>
</div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="padding-bottom:0.25em;background:lavender;">
<ul><li><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="180" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/16px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/23px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/31px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png 2x" title="Category" width="16"/> <a href="/wiki/Category:Infrastructure" title="Category:Infrastructure">Category</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg/28px-Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg/42px-Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg/56px-Nuvola_apps_kcmsystem.svg.png 2x" width="28"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Engineering" title="Portal:Engineering">Engineering portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Public_Infrastructure" title="Template:Public Infrastructure"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Public_Infrastructure" title="Template talk:Public Infrastructure"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Public_Infrastructure&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A <b>road</b> is a linear way for the conveyance of <a href="/wiki/Traffic" title="Traffic">traffic</a> that mostly has an <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">improved surface</a> for use by vehicles (motorized and non-motorized) and pedestrians. Unlike <a href="/wiki/Street" title="Street">streets</a>, the main function of roads is transportation.
</p><p>There are <a href="/wiki/Road_hierarchy" title="Road hierarchy">many types of roads</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Parkway" title="Parkway">parkways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avenue_(landscape)" title="Avenue (landscape)">avenues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">controlled-access highways</a> (freeways, motorways, and expressways), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tollway" title="Tollway">tollways</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate" title="Interstate">interstates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">highways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thoroughfare" title="Thoroughfare">thoroughfares</a>, and local roads.
</p><p>The primary features of roads include <a href="/wiki/Lane" title="Lane">lanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sidewalk" title="Sidewalk">sidewalks</a> (pavement), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roadway" title="Roadway">roadways</a> (carriageways), <a href="/wiki/Median_strip" title="Median strip">medians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shoulder_(road)" title="Shoulder (road)">shoulders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Road_verge" title="Road verge">verges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bike_path" title="Bike path">bike paths</a> (cycle paths), and <a href="/wiki/Shared-use_path" title="Shared-use path">shared-use paths</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Road_side_view_at_chalna,_Khulna_-_33.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Road_side_view_at_chalna%2C_Khulna_-_33.jpg/220px-Road_side_view_at_chalna%2C_Khulna_-_33.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Road_side_view_at_chalna%2C_Khulna_-_33.jpg/330px-Road_side_view_at_chalna%2C_Khulna_-_33.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Road_side_view_at_chalna%2C_Khulna_-_33.jpg/440px-Road_side_view_at_chalna%2C_Khulna_-_33.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Road_side_view_at_chalna,_Khulna_-_33.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A bricked road in Bangladesh</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gravel_road,_Namibia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Gravel_road%2C_Namibia.jpg/220px-Gravel_road%2C_Namibia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Gravel_road%2C_Namibia.jpg/330px-Gravel_road%2C_Namibia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Gravel_road%2C_Namibia.jpg/440px-Gravel_road%2C_Namibia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gravel_road,_Namibia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A gravel road in <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a></div></div></div>
<p>Historically many roads were simply recognizable routes without any formal construction or some maintenance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ways_of_the_World_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ways_of_the_World-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD) defines a road as "a line of communication (travelled way) using a stabilized base other than rails or air strips open to public traffic, primarily for the use of road motor vehicles running on their own wheels", which includes "bridges, tunnels, supporting structures, junctions, crossings, interchanges, and toll roads, but not cycle paths".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Transport_Forum" title="International Transport Forum">ITF</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNECE" title="UNECE">UNECE</a> <i>Glossary for Transport Statistics Illustrated</i> defines a road as a "Line of communication (traveled way) open to public traffic, primarily for the use of road motor vehicles, using a stabilized base other than rails or air strips. [...] Included are paved roads and other roads with a stabilized base, e.g. gravel roads. Roads also cover streets, bridges, tunnels, supporting structures, junctions, crossings and interchanges. Toll roads are also included. Excluded are dedicated cycle lanes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unece.org_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-unece.org-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1968 <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_on_Road_Traffic" title="Vienna Convention on Road Traffic">Vienna Convention on Road Traffic</a> defines a road as the entire surface of any way or street open to public traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>In urban areas roads may diverge through a city or village and be named as streets, serving a dual function as urban space <a href="/wiki/Easement" title="Easement">easement</a> and route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-difference_between_road_and_street_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-difference_between_road_and_street-5">[5]</a></sup> Modern roads are normally smoothed, paved, or otherwise prepared to allow easy travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RoadInfrastructureStrategicFrameworkforSouthAfrica_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-RoadInfrastructureStrategicFrameworkforSouthAfrica-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Australia" title="Highways in Australia">Highways in Australia</a></div>
<p>Part 2, Division 1, clauses 11-13 of the National Transport Commission Road Transport Legislation 2006 defines a road in Australia as 'an area that is open to or used by the public and is developed for, or has as one of its main uses, the driving or riding of motor vehicles.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Further, it defines a shoulder (typical an area of the road outside the edge line, or the curb) and a road-related area which includes green areas separating roads, areas designated for cyclists and areas generally accessible to the public for driving, riding or parking vehicles.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In New Zealand, the definition of a road is broad in common law<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> where the statutory definition includes areas the public has access to, by right or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Beaches, publicly accessible car parks and yards (even if privately owned), river beds, road shoulders (verges), wharves and bridges are included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> However, the definition of a road for insurance purposes may be restricted to reduce risk.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the United Kingdom <i><a href="/wiki/The_Highway_Code" title="The Highway Code">The Highway Code</a></i> details rules for "road users", but there is some ambiguity between the terms <i>highway</i> and <i>road</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> For the purposes of the <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highways_Act_1980" title="Highways Act 1980">Highways Act 1980</a>, which covers <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a> but not <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> or <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, road is "any length of highway or of any other road to which the public has access, and includes bridges over which a road passes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> This includes footpaths, bridleways and cycle tracks, and also road and driveways on private land and many car parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Direct_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Direct-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Excise_Duty" title="Vehicle Excise Duty">Vehicle Excise Duty</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Road_tax" title="Road tax">road use tax</a>, is payable on some vehicles used on the public road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Direct_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Direct-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>The definition of a road depends on the definition of a highway; there is no formal definition for a highway in the relevant Act. A 1984 ruling said "the land over which a public right of way exists is known as a highway; and although most highways have been made up into roads, and most easements of way exist over footpaths, the presence or absence of a made road has nothing to do with the distinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Another legal view is that while a highway historically included <a href="/wiki/Footpath" title="Footpath">footpaths</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridleway" title="Bridleway">bridleways</a>, driftways, etc., it can now be used to mean those ways that allow the movement of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motor_vehicles" title="Motor vehicles">motor vehicles</a>, and the term <i><a href="/wiki/Right-of-way_(transportation)" title="Right-of-way (transportation)">rights of way</a></i> can be used to cover the wider usage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the United States, laws distinguish between <i>public roads</i>, which are open to public use,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and <i>private roads</i>, which are privately controlled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_road_transport" title="History of road transport">History of road transport</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Gravel_road" title="Gravel road">Gravel road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trail" title="Trail">Trail</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Transfagarasan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Transfagarasan.jpg/170px-Transfagarasan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Transfagarasan.jpg/255px-Transfagarasan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Transfagarasan.jpg/340px-Transfagarasan.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Transfagarasan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Transf%C4%83g%C4%83r%C4%83%C8%99an" title="Transfăgărășan">Transfăgărășan</a> called "the best road in the world" by <a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV series)">Top Gear</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopGear_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-TopGear-19">[19]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG/220px-Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG/330px-Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG/440px-Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greek_street_-_III_century_BC_-_Porta_Rosa_-_Velia_-_Italy.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Porta Rosa, a Greek street dating from the 3rd to 4th century BC in <a href="/wiki/Velia" title="Velia">Velia</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">paved</a> surface and <a href="/wiki/Street_gutter" title="Street gutter">gutters</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PompeiiStreet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="795" data-file-width="594" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/PompeiiStreet.jpg/170px-PompeiiStreet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/PompeiiStreet.jpg/255px-PompeiiStreet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/PompeiiStreet.jpg/340px-PompeiiStreet.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PompeiiStreet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A paved Roman road in <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">Pompeii</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="1275" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg/220px-Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg/330px-Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg/440px-Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stora_tv%C3%A4rv%C3%A4gen_-_Ystad_11sep2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old tractor road over farmland, <a href="/wiki/Ystad" title="Ystad">Ystad</a>, Sweden</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%DA%A9%D9%88%D9%87%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%AC%D8%A7%D9%86_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg"><img alt="Ancient Sassanid Era Pathway in Behbahan, Persia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="330" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%DA%A9%D9%88%D9%87%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%AC%D8%A7%D9%86_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg/440px-%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%DA%A9%D9%88%D9%87%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%AC%D8%A7%D9%86_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sassanid</a> Era Pathway in <a href="/wiki/Behbahan" title="Behbahan">Behbahan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persia</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg"><img alt="Ancient Cobblestoned Road in Behbahan" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg/220px-%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg/330px-%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg/440px-%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D8%B3%D9%86%DA%AF%D9%81%D8%B1%D8%B4_%D8%B1%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86%DB%8C_%D8%AF%D8%B1_%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A8%D9%87%D8%A7%D9%86.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">Cobblestoned</a> Road in <a href="/wiki/Behbahan" title="Behbahan">Behbahan</a></div></div></div>
<p>The assertion that the first pathways were the <a href="/wiki/Trail" title="Trail">trails</a> made by animals has not been universally accepted; in many cases animals do not follow constant paths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ways_of_the_World_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ways_of_the_World-1">[1]</a></sup> Some believe that some roads originated from following animal trails.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wheathampstead_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-wheathampstead-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Icknield_Way" title="Icknield Way">Icknield Way</a> may exemplify this type of road origination, where human and animal both selected the same natural line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Icknield_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Icknield-22">[22]</a></sup> By about 10,000 BC human travelers used rough roads/pathways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ways_of_the_World_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ways_of_the_World-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The world's oldest known paved road was constructed in Egypt some time between 2600 and 2200 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">Stone</a>-paved streets appear in the city of <a href="/wiki/Ur" title="Ur">Ur</a> in the Middle East dating back to 4000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ways_of_the_World_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ways_of_the_World-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Corduroy_road" title="Corduroy road">Corduroy roads</a> (log roads) are found dating to 4000 BC in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glastonbury,_England" title="Glastonbury, England">Glastonbury</a>, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ways_of_the_World_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ways_of_the_World-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Track" title="Sweet Track">Sweet Track</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timber_trackway" title="Timber trackway">timber track</a> causeway in England, is one of the oldest engineered roads discovered and the oldest timber trackway discovered in Northern Europe. Built in winter 3807 BC or spring 3806 BC, (tree-ring dating – <a href="/wiki/Dendrochronology" title="Dendrochronology">dendrochronology</a> – enabled very precise dating). It was claimed to be the oldest road in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Current_Archaeology_172_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Current_Archaeology_172-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highways:_The_Location_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Highways:_The_Location-25">[25]</a></sup> until the 2009 discovery of a 6,000-year-old trackway in <a href="/wiki/Plumstead" title="Plumstead">Plumstead</a>, London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>Brick-paved streets appeared in India as early as 3000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ways_of_the_World_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ways_of_the_World-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1995 BC: an early subdividing of roadways evidenced with <a href="/wiki/Sidewalk" title="Sidewalk">sidewalks</a> built in Anatolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 500 BC, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darius_I_the_Great" title="Darius I the Great">Darius I the Great</a> started an extensive road system for the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> (Persia), including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Road" title="Royal Road">Royal Road</a>, which was one of the finest highways of its time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RoyalRoad_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-RoyalRoad-29">[29]</a></sup> connecting <a href="/wiki/Sardis" title="Sardis">Sardis</a> (the westernmost major city of the empire) to <a href="/wiki/Susa" title="Susa">Susa</a>. The road remained in use after Roman times. These road systems reached as far east as <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactria</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>In ancient times, transport by river was far easier and faster than transport by road,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highways:_The_Location_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Highways:_The_Location-25">[25]</a></sup> especially considering the cost of road construction and the difference in carrying capacity between <a href="/wiki/Cart" title="Cart">carts</a> and river <a href="/wiki/Barge" title="Barge">barges</a>. A hybrid of road transport and ship transport beginning in about 1740 is the <a href="/wiki/Horse-drawn_boat" title="Horse-drawn boat">horse-drawn boat</a> in which the horse follows a cleared path along the river bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-horseboating_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-horseboating-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HorseDrawnBoats_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-HorseDrawnBoats-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li>From about 312 BC, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> built straight<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Discovering_Roman_Technology_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Discovering_Roman_Technology-33">[33]</a></sup> strong stone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_road" title="Roman road">Roman roads</a> throughout Europe and North Africa, in support of its military campaigns. At its peak the Roman Empire was connected by 29 major roads moving out from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a> and covering 78,000 kilometers or 52,964 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_mile" title="Roman mile">Roman miles</a> of paved roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highways:_The_Location_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Highways:_The_Location-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the 8th century AD, many roads were built throughout the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Arab Empire</a>. The most sophisticated roads were those in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, which were paved with <a href="/wiki/Tar" title="Tar">tar</a>. Tar was derived from petroleum, accessed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_field" title="Oil field">oil fields</a> in the region, through the chemical process of <a href="/wiki/Destructive_distillation" title="Destructive distillation">destructive distillation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajram_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ajram-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Highways_Act_1555" title="Highways Act 1555">Highways Act 1555</a> in Britain transferred responsibility for maintaining roads from government to local parishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highways:_The_Location_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-Highways:_The_Location-25">[25]</a></sup> This resulted in a poor and variable state of roads. To remedy this, the first of the <a href="/wiki/Turnpike_trust" title="Turnpike trust">turnpike trusts</a> was established around 1706, to build good roads and collect tolls from passing vehicles. Eventually there were approximately 1,100 trusts in Britain and some 36,800 km (22,870 miles) of engineered roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highways:_The_Location_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-Highways:_The_Location-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Riots" title="Rebecca Riots">Rebecca Riots</a> in Carmarthenshire and <a href="/wiki/Rhayader" title="Rhayader">Rhayader</a> from 1839 to 1844 contributed to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Commission" title="Royal Commission">Royal Commission</a> that led to the demise of the system in 1844,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Victorian_Powys_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Victorian_Powys-35">[35]</a></sup> which coincided with the <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Great_Britain_to_1830" title="History of rail transport in Great Britain to 1830">development of the UK railway system</a>.</li>
<li>In the late-19th century roading engineers began to cater for cyclists by building separate lanes alongside roadways.</li>
<li>From the beginning of the 20th century, roads were increasingly built for tourism and also to create jobs. A typical example of the stimulation of tourism is the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Strada_Statale_48_Delle_Dolomiti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Strada Statale 48 Delle Dolomiti (page does not exist)">Great Dolomite Road</a>, while the creation of the panoramic coastal road <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Strada_Costiera&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Strada Costiera (page does not exist)">Strada Costiera</a> between <a href="/wiki/Duino" title="Duino">Duino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barcola" title="Barcola">Barcola</a> in 1928 was very much focused on creating jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG/170px-Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG/255px-Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG/340px-Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kantatie_65_at_Tampere.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A highway in <a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a> (<a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Road design is part of <a href="/wiki/Highway_engineering" title="Highway engineering">highway engineering</a>. <a href="/wiki/Structural_road_design" title="Structural road design">Structural road design</a> is designing a road for the environment in order to extend its longevity and reduce maintenance. The <a href="/wiki/Shell_pavement_design_method" title="Shell pavement design method">Shell pavement design method</a> is used in many countries for the design of new asphalt roadsides.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_road_transport_terms" title="Glossary of road transport terms">Glossary of road transport terms</a></div>
<dl><dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adverse_camber" title="Adverse camber">Adverse camber</a></dt>
<dd>Where a road slopes towards the outside of a bend, increasing the likelihood that vehicles travelling at speed will skid or topple. Usually only a temporary situation during road maintenance.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Geometric_design_of_roads#Alignment" title="Geometric design of roads">Alignment</a></dt>
<dd>The route of the road, defined as a series of horizontal tangents and curves.</dd>
<dt>All-weather road</dt>
<dd>Unpaved road that is constructed of a material that does not create mud during rainfall.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Banked_turn" title="Banked turn">Banked turn</a></dt>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belisha_Beacon" title="Belisha Beacon">Belisha Beacon</a></dt>
<dd>An orange globe, lit at night, used to highlight a pedestrian crossing</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Bicycle_boulevard" title="Bicycle boulevard">Bicycle boulevard</a></dt>
<dd>A street that allows local vehicle traffic, but is prioritized for bicycles and other non-motorized travel</dd>
<dt><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle,_NSW_in_Australia.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle%2C_NSW_in_Australia.JPG/170px-Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle%2C_NSW_in_Australia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle%2C_NSW_in_Australia.JPG/255px-Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle%2C_NSW_in_Australia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle%2C_NSW_in_Australia.JPG/340px-Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle%2C_NSW_in_Australia.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roads_to_Beaches_of_Newcastle,_NSW_in_Australia.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A beach road (Newcastle, NSW, Australia)</div></div></div></dt>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Bollard#Roads" title="Bollard">Bollard</a></dt>
<dd>Rigid posts that can be arranged in a line to close a road or path to vehicles above a certain width</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Byway_(road)" title="Byway (road)">Byway</a></dt>
<dd>Highway over which the public have <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_way_in_England_and_Wales" title="Rights of way in England and Wales">a right to travel</a> for vehicular and other kinds of traffic, but is used mainly as a footpath or bridleway</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Bypass_(road)" title="Bypass (road)">Bypass</a></dt>
<dd>Road that avoids or "bypasses" a built-up area, town, or village</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bottleneck_(traffic)" title="Bottleneck (traffic)">Bottleneck</a></dt>
<dd>Section of a road with a carrying capacity substantially below that of other sections of the same road</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Botts%27_dots" title="Botts' dots">Botts' dots</a></dt>
<dd>Non-reflective <a href="/wiki/Raised_pavement_marker" title="Raised pavement marker">raised pavement marker</a> used on roads</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Camber_angle#Road_camber" title="Camber angle">Camber</a> (or crown)</dt>
<dd>The slope of the <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">road surface</a> downwards away from the centre of the road, so that surface water can flow freely to the edge of the carriageway, or on bends angling of the surface to lean traffic 'into the bend' reducing the chance of a skid.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Cant_(road/rail)#Roads" title="Cant (road/rail)">Cant</a></dt>
<dd>Another name for cross slope or camber</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Carriageway" title="Carriageway">Carriageway</a></dt>
<dd>Part of the road intended for the movement of road motor vehicles; the parts of the road which form a shoulder for the lower or upper layers of the road surface are not part of the roadway, nor are those parts of the road intended for the circulation of road vehicles which are not self-propelled or for the parking of vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unece.org_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-unece.org-3">[3]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_eye_(road)" title="Cat's eye (road)">Cat's eye</a></dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Reflection_(physics)" title="Reflection (physics)">Reflective</a> <a href="/wiki/Raised_pavement_marker" title="Raised pavement marker">raised pavement marker</a> used on roads</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Chicane" title="Chicane">Chicane</a></dt>
<dd>Sequence of tight serpentine curves (usually an S-shape curve or a bus stop)</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Chipseal" title="Chipseal">Chipseal</a></dt>
<dd>Road surface composed of a thin layer of crushed stone 'chips' and asphalt emulsion. It seals the surface and protects it from weather, but provides no structural strength. It is cheaper than <a href="/wiki/Asphalt_concrete" title="Asphalt concrete">asphalt concrete</a> or concrete. In the United States, it is usually only used on low volume rural roads</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Corniche" title="Corniche">Corniche</a></dt>
<dd>Road on the side of a cliff or mountain, with the ground rising on one side and falling away on the other</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Cross_slope" title="Cross slope">Cross slope</a></dt>
<dd>The <a href="/wiki/Slope" title="Slope">slope</a> of the pavement, expressed as units of rise per unit of run, or as a percentage</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curb_(road)" title="Curb (road)">Curb</a> (kerb)</dt>
<dd>A raised edge at the side of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roadway" title="Roadway">roadway</a>.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Curb_extension" title="Curb extension">Curb extension</a></dt>
<dd>(also kerb extension, bulb-out, nib, elephant ear, curb bulge and blister) <a href="/wiki/Traffic_calming" title="Traffic calming">Traffic calming</a> measure, intended to slow the speed of traffic and increase driver awareness, particularly in built-up and residential <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighborhoods" title="Neighborhoods">neighborhoods</a>.</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cycle_lane" title="Cycle lane">Cycle lane</a></dt>
<dd>Part of a carriageway designated for cycles and distinguished from the rest of the carriageway by longitudinal road markings. Mopeds may also be allowed to use a cycle lane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unece.org_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-unece.org-3">[3]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Cycle_track" title="Cycle track">Cycle track</a></dt>
<dd>Independent road or part of a road designated for cycles and sign-posted as such. A cycle track is separated from other roads or other parts of the same road by structural means. Mopeds may also be allowed to use the cycle track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unece.org_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-unece.org-3">[3]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Cycling_infrastructure" title="Cycling infrastructure">Cycling infrastructure</a></dt>
<dd>Cycling-friendly infrastructure integrated into the roadway or in its own right of way</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Drainage_gradient" title="Drainage gradient">Drainage gradient</a></dt>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Farm-to-market_road" title="Farm-to-market road">Farm-to-market road</a></dt>
<dd>A state road or county road that connects rural or agricultural areas to market towns.</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fork_(road)" title="Fork (road)">Fork</a></dt>
<dd>(literally "fork in the road") Type of <a href="/wiki/Intersection_(road)" title="Intersection (road)">intersection</a> where a road splits</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Grade_(slope)#Roads" title="Grade (slope)">Grade</a></dt>
<dd>Longitudinal slope</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Green_lane_(road)" title="Green lane (road)">Green lane</a></dt>
<dd>(UK) Unsurfaced road, may be so infrequently used that vegetation colonises freely, hence 'green'. Many green lanes are ancient routes that have existed for millennia.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Guide_rail" title="Guide rail">Guide rail</a></dt>
<dd>Prevents vehicles from veering off the road into oncoming traffic, crashing against solid objects or falling from a road. Also called a <a href="/wiki/Guard_rail" title="Guard rail">guard rail</a> or <a href="/wiki/Traffic_barrier" title="Traffic barrier">traffic barrier</a>.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Street_gutter" title="Street gutter">Gutter</a></dt>
<dd>A drainage channel usually at the edge of the road or along a median.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">Interstate Highway System</a> (United States)</dt>
<dd>System of Interstate and Defense Highways</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Lane" title="Lane">Lane</a></dt>
<dd>One of the longitudinal strips into which a carriageway is divisible, whether or not defined by longitudinal road markings, which is wide enough for one moving line of motor vehicles other than motorcycles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unece.org_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-unece.org-3">[3]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Layby" title="Layby">Layby</a> (Pullout, pull-off)</dt>
<dd>A paved area beside a <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">main road</a> where <a href="/wiki/Car" title="Car">cars</a> can stop temporarily to let another car pass.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Loose_chippings" title="Loose chippings">Loose chippings</a></dt>
<dd>The hazard of stone chippings that have come loose</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Median_strip" title="Median strip">Median</a></dt>
<dd>On <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">dual carriageway</a> roads, including <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">controlled-access highways</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divided_highway" title="Divided highway">divided highways</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Limited-access_road" title="Limited-access road">limited-access roads</a>, the central reservation (<a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>), median (<a href="/wiki/North_American_English" title="North American English">North American English</a>), median strip (North American English and <a href="/wiki/Australian_English" title="Australian English">Australian English</a>), neutral ground [Louisiana English] or central nature strip (Australian English): Area that separates opposing <a href="/wiki/Lane" title="Lane">lanes</a> of traffic</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorway" title="Motorway">Motorway</a></dt>
<dd>(Europe) (Freeways in the US, Special road in the UK) Road, specially designed and built for motor traffic, which does not serve properties bordering on it, with separate carriageways for traffic in two directions, with no crossings at the same level (road, railway, tramway track, or footpath) and sign-posted as a motorway and is reserved for specific categories of road motor vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unece.org_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-unece.org-3">[3]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Mountain_pass" title="Mountain pass">Mountain pass</a></dt>
<dd>A relatively low-level route through a range of mountains</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Milestone" title="Milestone">Milestone</a></dt>
<dd>One of a series of numbered markers placed along a road, often at regular intervals, showing the distance to destinations.</dd>
<dt>National Highway</dt>
<dd>Road built and maintained by a national authority.</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pavement_(material)" title="Pavement (material)">Pavement</a></dt>
<dd>The road regarded as a geoconstruction. In the UK the term is <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">road surface</a> and the pavement is a pedestrian walkway alongside the road.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_crossing" title="Pedestrian crossing">Pedestrian crossing</a></dt>
<dd>Designated point on a road where road marking or other means helps pedestrians cross safely</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Pelican_crossing" title="Pelican crossing">Pelican crossing</a></dt>
<dd>(officially <i>Pelicon crossing</i>) (UK) A PEdestrian LIght CONtrolled crossing.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Private_highway" title="Private highway">Private highway</a></dt>
<dd>Highway owned and operated for profit by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_industry" title="Private industry">private industry</a></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Private_road" title="Private road">Private road</a></dt>
<dd>Road owned and maintained by a private individual, organization, or company rather than by a government</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Geometric_design_of_roads#Profile" title="Geometric design of roads">Profile</a></dt>
<dd>The vertical alignment of a road, expressed as a series of grades, connected by parabolic curves.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Protected_intersection" title="Protected intersection">Protected Intersections for Bicycles</a></dt>
<dd>A much safer design with a corner refuge island, a setback crossing of the pedestrians and <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cyclists</a>, generally between 1.5–7 metres of setback, a forward stop bar, which allows cyclists to stop for a <a href="/wiki/Traffic_light" title="Traffic light">traffic light</a> well ahead of motor traffic who must stop behind the crosswalk. Separate signal staging or at least an advance green for cyclists and pedestrians is used to give cyclists and pedestrians no conflicts or a head start over traffic. The design makes a right turn on red, and sometimes left on red depending on the geometry of the intersection in question, possible in many cases, often without stopping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_Path" title="Bicycle Path">Protected Bicycle Path</a></dt>
<dd>Cyclists ideally have a protected bike lane on separated by a concrete median with splay <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerb" title="Kerb">kerbs</a> if possible, and have a protected bike lane width of at least 2 metres if possible (one way). In the Netherlands, most one-way cycle paths are at least 2.5 metres wide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bicycledutch.wordpress.com_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-bicycledutch.wordpress.com-39">[39]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Public_space" title="Public space">Public space</a></dt>
<dd>Place where anyone has a right to come without being excluded because of <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomics" title="Socioeconomics">economic or social</a> conditions</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ranch_road" title="Ranch road">Ranch road</a></dt>
<dd>U.S. road that connects rural and agricultural areas to <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market towns</a></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Route_number" title="Route number">Road number</a></dt>
<dd>Often assigned to identify a stretch of public roads – often dependent on the <a href="/wiki/Types_of_road" title="Types of road">type of road</a>, with numbers differentiating between <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">interstates</a>, motorways, <a href="/wiki/Arterial_road" title="Arterial road">arterial thoroughfares</a>, etc.</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road-traffic_safety" title="Road-traffic safety">Road-traffic safety</a></dt>
<dd>Process to reduce the harm (deaths, injuries, and property damage) that result from vehicle crashes on public roads</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Roadworks" title="Roadworks">Roadworks</a></dt>
<dd>Part or all of the road is occupied for work or maintenance</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Surface_roughness" title="Surface roughness">Roughness</a></dt>
<dd>Deviations from a true planar pavement surface, which affects vehicle suspension deflection, dynamic loading, <a href="/wiki/Ride_quality" title="Ride quality">ride quality</a>, surface drainage and winter operations. Roughness have wavelengths ranging from 500 mm up to some 40 m. The upper limit may be as high as 350 m when considering motion sickness aspects; motion sickness is generated by motion with down to 0.1 Hz frequency; in an ambulance car driving 78 mph (126 km/h), waves with up to 350 m will excite motion sickness.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">Roundabout</a></dt>
<dd>A road junction where typically three or more roads are joined by a circular section of road. Traffic 'on the roundabout' has priority over traffic on approach roads, unless indicated otherwise. In countries where traffic drives on the left the roundabout is traveled in a clockwise direction. Also known as an <i>island</i> in parts of the UK.</dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_path" title="Bicycle path">Segregated Bicycle Path</a></dt>
<dd>Cyclists ideally have a protected bike lane separated by a concrete median with splay <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerb" title="Kerb">kerbs</a> if possible, and have a protected bike lane width of at least 2 meters if possible (one way). In the Netherlands, most one-way cycle paths are at least 2.5 metres wide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bicycledutch.wordpress.com_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-bicycledutch.wordpress.com-39">[39]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Shoulder_(road)" title="Shoulder (road)">Shoulder</a> (also hard shoulder)</dt>
<dd>A clear, level area to the side of the roadway available for stopping if needed.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/State_highway" title="State highway">State highway</a></dt>
<dd>Road numbered by the state, falling below numbered national highways (like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Numbered_Highways" title="United States Numbered Highways">U.S. Routes</a>) in the hierarchy <i>or</i> a road maintained by the state, including nationally numbered highways</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Traffic" title="Traffic">Traffic</a></dt>
<dd>Pedestrians, ridden or herded animals, vehicles, bicycles, and other conveyances using any road for purposes of travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texture_(roads)" title="Texture (roads)">Texture (roads)</a></dt>
<dd>Deviations from a true planar pavement surface, which affects the interaction between road and tire. Microtexture have wavelengths below 0.5 mm, Macrotexture below 50 mm and Megatexture below 500 mm.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Traffic_calming" title="Traffic calming">Traffic calming</a></dt>
<dd>Set of strategies used by <a href="/wiki/Urban_planner" title="Urban planner">urban planners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_engineering_(transportation)" title="Traffic engineering (transportation)">traffic engineers</a> to slow down or reduce motor vehicle traffic, thereby improving safety for pedestrians and <a href="/wiki/Bicycle-friendly" title="Bicycle-friendly">bicyclists</a> and improving the environment for residents</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Traffic_island" title="Traffic island">Traffic island</a></dt>
<dd>(UK) A small raised area used to help define the traffic flow, which may also act as a refuge for pedestrians crossing the carriageway or a location for signs, barriers or lights – a synonym for <a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">roundabout</a> in some parts of the UK</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Traffic_light" title="Traffic light">Traffic light</a></dt>
<dd>Also known as a traffic signal, stop light, stop-and-go lights – a signaling device at a road intersection, pedestrian crossing, or other location that assigns right of way to different approaches to an intersection</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Zebra_crossing" title="Zebra crossing">Zebra crossing</a> (UK)</dt>
<dd>A pedestrian crossing marked by black and white stripes on the carriageway</dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Roadworks" title="Roadworks">Roadworks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macadam" title="Macadam">Macadam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Track_bed" title="Track bed">Track bed</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MortarlessPavement.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1008" data-file-width="1497" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/MortarlessPavement.jpg/220px-MortarlessPavement.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/MortarlessPavement.jpg/330px-MortarlessPavement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/MortarlessPavement.jpg/440px-MortarlessPavement.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MortarlessPavement.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Layers in the construction of a mortarless pavement: A.) <a href="/wiki/Subgrade" title="Subgrade">Subgrade</a> B.) <a href="/wiki/Subbase_(pavement)" title="Subbase (pavement)">Subbase</a> C.) <a href="/wiki/Base_course" title="Base course">Base course</a> D.) <a href="/wiki/Paver_base" title="Paver base">Paver base</a> E.) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paver_(flooring)" title="Paver (flooring)">Pavers</a> F.) Fine-grained <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transport_engineering" title="Transport engineering">transport engineering</a>, <b>subgrade</b> is the native material underneath a constructed road.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank,_California.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="5000" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank%2C_California.JPG/220px-Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank%2C_California.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank%2C_California.JPG/330px-Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank%2C_California.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank%2C_California.JPG/440px-Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank%2C_California.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burbank_Ave_I-5_overpass_under_construction_in_Burbank,_California.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Overpass" title="Overpass">Overpass</a> under construction over <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5_in_California" title="Interstate 5 in California">Interstate 5</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank, California</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Us_land_survey_officer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="328" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Us_land_survey_officer.jpg/220px-Us_land_survey_officer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Us_land_survey_officer.jpg/330px-Us_land_survey_officer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Us_land_survey_officer.jpg/440px-Us_land_survey_officer.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Us_land_survey_officer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Surveyor at work with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leveling_instrument" title="Leveling instrument">leveling instrument</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1895" data-file-width="2171" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg/220px-Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg/330px-Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg/440px-Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Road_building-Hungary-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Asphalt layer and <a href="/wiki/Hamm_AG" title="Hamm AG">Hamm</a> <a href="/wiki/Road_roller" title="Road roller">road roller</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG/220px-Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG/330px-Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG/440px-Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Motorway_construction_in_Ireland.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Subbase_(pavement)" title="Subbase (pavement)">Sub-base layer</a> composed of cement-based material being applied during construction of the <a href="/wiki/M8_motorway_(Ireland)" title="M8 motorway (Ireland)">M8 motorway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Motorways_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Motorways in the Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3246" data-file-width="4774" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg/220px-MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg/330px-MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg/440px-MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MyanmarRoadConstruction2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Road construction in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg/220px-Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg/330px-Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg/440px-Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clearing_rocks_from_mountain_road._Spiti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clearing rocks from mountain road in <a href="/wiki/Spiti" title="Spiti">Spiti</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Road construction</b> requires the creation of an <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">engineered</a> continuous right-of-way or <b>roadbed</b>, overcoming geographic obstacles and having <a href="/wiki/Grade_(slope)" title="Grade (slope)">grades</a> low enough to permit vehicle or <a href="/wiki/Walking" title="Walking">foot travel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kitsap_County_Road_Standards_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kitsap_County_Road_Standards-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 15">: 15 </span></sup> and may be required to meet standards set by law<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MRSC_road_standards_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-MRSC_road_standards-44">[44]</a></sup> or official guidelines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup> The process is often begun with the removal of earth and rock by digging or blasting, construction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embankment_(transportation)" title="Embankment (transportation)">embankments</a>, bridges and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tunnels" title="Tunnels">tunnels</a>, and removal of vegetation (this may involve <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>) and followed by the laying of pavement material. A variety of <a href="/wiki/Heavy_equipment" title="Heavy equipment">road building equipment</a> is employed in road building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caterpillar_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caterpillar-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Volvo_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Volvo-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>After design, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Approval_rating" title="Approval rating">approval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Planning" title="Planning">planning</a>, legal, and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy" title="Environmental policy">environmental</a> considerations have been addressed alignment of the road is set out by a <a href="/wiki/Surveying" title="Surveying">surveyor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Discovering_Roman_Technology_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Discovering_Roman_Technology-33">[33]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radius_of_curvature_(mathematics)" title="Radius of curvature (mathematics)">radii</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slope" title="Slope">gradient</a> are designed and staked out to best suit the natural ground levels and minimize the amount of cut and fill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 34">: 34 </span></sup> Great care is taken to preserve reference <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(surveying)" title="Benchmark (surveying)">Benchmarks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 59">: 59 </span></sup>
</p><p>Roads are designed and built for primary use by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vehicular" title="Vehicular">vehicular</a> and pedestrian traffic. <a href="/wiki/Storm_drain" title="Storm drain">Storm drainage</a> and environmental considerations are a major concern. <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">Erosion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediment</a> controls are constructed to prevent detrimental effects. Drainage lines are laid with <a href="/wiki/Seal_(mechanical)" title="Seal (mechanical)">sealed</a> joints in the road easement with runoff <a href="/wiki/Coefficient" title="Coefficient">coefficients</a> and characteristics adequate for the <a href="/wiki/Zoning" title="Zoning">land zoning</a> and storm water system. Drainage systems must be capable of carrying the ultimate design flow from the upstream catchment with approval for the outfall from the appropriate authority to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watercourse" title="Watercourse">watercourse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stream" title="Stream">creek</a>, river or the sea for drainage discharge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 38–40">: 38–40 </span></sup>
</p><p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borrow_pit" title="Borrow pit">borrow pit</a> (source for obtaining fill, gravel, and rock) and a water source should be located near or in reasonable distance to the road construction site. Approval from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_authorities" title="Local authorities">local authorities</a> may be required to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_well" title="Water well">draw water</a> or for working (crushing and screening) of materials for construction needs. The <a href="/wiki/Topsoil" title="Topsoil">topsoil</a> and vegetation is removed from the borrow pit and stockpiled for subsequent <a href="/wiki/Land_rehabilitation" title="Land rehabilitation">rehabilitation</a> of the extraction area. Side slopes in the excavation area not steeper than one vertical to two horizontal for safety reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 53–56">: 53–56 </span></sup>
</p><p>Old road surfaces, fences, and buildings may need to be removed before construction can begin. Trees in the road construction area may be marked for retention. These protected trees should not have the topsoil within the area of the tree's drip line removed and the area should be kept clear of construction material and equipment. Compensation or replacement may be required if a protected tree is damaged. Much of the vegetation may be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mulched" title="Mulched">mulched</a> and put aside for use during reinstatement. The topsoil is usually stripped and stockpiled nearby for rehabilitation of newly constructed embankments along the road. Stumps and roots are removed and holes filled as required before the earthwork begins. Final rehabilitation after road construction is completed will include seeding, planting, watering and other activities to reinstate the area to be consistent with the untouched surrounding areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 66–67">: 66–67 </span></sup>
</p><p>Processes during earthwork include excavation, removal of material to spoil, filling, compacting, construction and trimming. If rock or other unsuitable material is discovered it is removed, moisture content is managed and replaced with standard fill compacted to meet the design requirements (generally 90–95% relative compaction). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_blasting" title="Rock blasting">Blasting</a> is not frequently used to excavate the roadbed as the intact rock structure forms an ideal road base. When a depression must be filled to come up to the road grade the native bed is compacted after the topsoil has been removed. The fill is made by the "compacted layer method" where a layer of fill is spread then compacted to specifications, under saturated conditions. The process is repeated until the desired grade is reached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 68–69">: 68–69 </span></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PavementStratum.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3488" data-file-width="2616" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/PavementStratum.JPG/170px-PavementStratum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/PavementStratum.JPG/255px-PavementStratum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/PavementStratum.JPG/340px-PavementStratum.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PavementStratum.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical pavement strata for a heavily traveled road</div></div></div>
<p>General <a href="/wiki/Fill_dirt" title="Fill dirt">fill material</a> should be free of <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organics</a>, meet minimum <a href="/wiki/California_bearing_ratio" title="California bearing ratio">California bearing ratio</a> (CBR) results and have a low <a href="/wiki/Atterberg_limits#Plasticity_index" title="Atterberg limits">plasticity index</a>. The lower fill generally comprises sand or a sand-rich mixture with fine gravel, which acts as an inhibitor to the growth of plants or other vegetable matter. The compacted fill also serves as lower-stratum drainage. Select second fill (<a href="/wiki/Sieve" title="Sieve">sieved</a>) should be composed of <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravel</a>, decomposed <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">rock</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crushed_rock" title="Crushed rock">broken rock</a> below a specified <a href="/wiki/Particle_size" title="Particle size">particle size</a> and be free of large lumps of <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a>. <a href="/wiki/Loam" title="Loam">Sand clay</a> fill may also be used. The roadbed must be "proof rolled" after each layer of fill is compacted. If a <a href="/wiki/Road_roller" title="Road roller">roller</a> passes over an area without creating visible deformation or spring the section is deemed to comply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thelastfrontier_45-7"><a href="#cite_note-thelastfrontier-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 70–72">: 70–72 </span></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Geosynthetics" title="Geosynthetics">Geosynthetics</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geotextiles" title="Geotextiles">geotextiles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geogrids" title="Geogrids">geogrids</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cellular_confinement" title="Cellular confinement">geocells</a> are frequently used in the various pavement layers to improve road quality. These materials and methods are used in low-traffic private roadways as well as public roads and highways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mainland_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mainland-48">[48]</a></sup> Geosynthetics perform four main functions in roads: separation, reinforcement, filtration, and drainage; which increase the pavement performance, reduce construction costs and decrease maintenance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Self-published_sources" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on a self-published source. (December 2017)">self-published source</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The completed roadway is finished by paving or left with a gravel or other <a href="/wiki/Dirt_road" title="Dirt road">natural</a> surface. The <a href="/wiki/Types_of_road" title="Types of road">type of road</a> surface is dependent on economic factors and expected usage. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road-traffic_safety" title="Road-traffic safety">Safety</a> improvements such as <a href="/wiki/Traffic_sign" title="Traffic sign">traffic signs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crash_barrier" title="Crash barrier">crash barriers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raised_pavement_marker" title="Raised pavement marker">raised pavement markers</a> and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Road_surface_marking" title="Road surface marking">road surface marking</a> are installed.
</p><p>According to a May 2009 report by the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_State_Highway_and_Transportation_Officials" title="American Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials">American Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials</a> (AASHTO) and TRIP – a national transportation research organization – driving on rough roads costs the average American motorist approximately $400 a year in extra vehicle operating costs. Drivers living in urban areas with populations more than 250,000 are paying upwards of $750 more annually because of accelerated vehicle deterioration, increased maintenance, additional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuel_consumption" title="Fuel consumption">fuel consumption</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tire_wear" title="Tire wear">tire wear</a> caused by poor road conditions.
</p><p>When a <a href="/wiki/Single_carriageway" title="Single carriageway">single carriageway</a> road is converted into dual carriageway by building a second separate carriageway alongside the first, it is usually referred to as <i>duplication</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> <i>twinning</i> or <i>doubling</i>. The original carriageway is changed from two-way to become one-way, while the new carriageway is one-way in the opposite direction. In the same way as converting railway lines from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_track_(rail)" title="Single track (rail)">single track</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_track" title="Double track">double track</a>, the new carriageway is not always constructed directly alongside the existing carriageway.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reallocation">Reallocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Reallocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modal_shift" title="Modal shift">Modal shift</a> and <a href="/wiki/Car-free_movement" title="Car-free movement">Car-free movement</a></div>
<p>Roads that are intended for use by a particular mode of transport can be reallocated for another mode of transport,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> i.e. by using <a href="/wiki/Traffic_sign" title="Traffic sign">traffic signs</a>. For instance, in the ongoing road space reallocation effort, some roads (particularly in city centers) which are intended for use by <a href="/wiki/Car" title="Car">cars</a> are increasingly being repurposed for <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Walking" title="Walking">walking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance">Maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Roadworks" title="Roadworks">Roadworks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Road_surface#Surface_deterioration" title="Road surface">Road surface § Surface deterioration</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baustelle.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="613" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Baustelle.svg/170px-Baustelle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Baustelle.svg/255px-Baustelle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Baustelle.svg/340px-Baustelle.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baustelle.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Road works ahead" sign, typically used in Europe</div></div></div>
<p>Like all structures, roads deteriorate over time.
