Deterioration is primarily due to environmental effects such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frost_heave" title="Frost heave">frost heaves</a>, thermal cracking and oxidation often contribute, however accumulated damage from vehicles also contributes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frost_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-frost-55">[55]</a></sup> According to a series of experiments carried out in the late 1950s, called the <a href="/wiki/AASHO_Road_Test" title="AASHO Road Test">AASHO Road Test</a>, it was empirically determined that the effective damage done to the road is roughly proportional to the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_power" title="Fourth power">fourth power</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_axle_weight_rating" title="Gross axle weight rating">axle weight</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motorway_Achievement_Pg252_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Motorway_Achievement_Pg252-56">[56]</a></sup> A typical <a href="/wiki/Semi-trailer_truck" title="Semi-trailer truck">tractor-trailer</a> weighing 80,000 <a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">pounds</a> (36.287 <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">t</a>) with 8,000 pounds (3.629 t) on the steer axle and 36,000 pounds (16.329 t) on both of the tandem axle groups is expected to do 7,800 times more damage than a passenger vehicle with 2,000 pounds (0.907 t) on each axle. <a href="/wiki/Pothole" title="Pothole">Potholes</a> on roads are caused by rain damage and vehicle braking or related construction works.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3912" data-file-width="2256" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG/170px-Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG/255px-Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG/340px-Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Making_lines_on_the_road.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Line marking in rural India</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">Pavements</a> are designed for an expected <a href="/wiki/Service_life" title="Service life">service life</a> or <a href="/wiki/Design_life" title="Design life">design life</a>. In some parts of the United Kingdom the standard design life is 40 years for new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitumen" title="Bitumen">bitumen</a> and concrete pavement. Maintenance is considered in the whole life cost of the road with service at 10, 20 and 30 year milestones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highways_The_Location_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Highways_The_Location-57">[57]</a></sup> Roads can be and are designed for a variety of lives (8-, 15-, 30-, and 60-year designs). When pavement lasts longer than its intended life, it may have been overbuilt, and the original costs may have been too high. When a pavement fails before its intended design life, the owner may have excessive repair and rehabilitation costs. Some <a href="/wiki/Asphalt_concrete" title="Asphalt concrete">asphalt</a> pavements are designed as <i>perpetual pavements</i> with an expected structural life in excess of 50 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parking_bay_white_line_detail,_Tesco,_Oban,_July_2020.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parking_bay_white_line_detail%2C_Tesco%2C_Oban%2C_July_2020.jpg/220px-Parking_bay_white_line_detail%2C_Tesco%2C_Oban%2C_July_2020.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parking_bay_white_line_detail%2C_Tesco%2C_Oban%2C_July_2020.jpg/330px-Parking_bay_white_line_detail%2C_Tesco%2C_Oban%2C_July_2020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parking_bay_white_line_detail%2C_Tesco%2C_Oban%2C_July_2020.jpg/440px-Parking_bay_white_line_detail%2C_Tesco%2C_Oban%2C_July_2020.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parking_bay_white_line_detail,_Tesco,_Oban,_July_2020.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A white line used to designate a parking bay in Scotland. The line has deteriorated to the point that both an older yellow line and the underlying surface are visible beneath.</div></div></div>
<p>Many asphalt pavements built over 35 years ago, despite not being specifically designed as a perpetual pavement, have remained in good condition long past their design life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Many concrete pavements built since the 1950s have significantly outlived their intended design lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Map_Future_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Map_Future-60">[60]</a></sup> Some roads like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Wacker_Drive" title="Wacker Drive">Wacker Drive</a>, a major two-level (and at one point, three-level) roadway in the downtown area, are being rebuilt with a designed service life of 100 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fly_Ash_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fly_Ash-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Virtually all roads require some form of maintenance before they come to the end of their service life. Pro-active agencies use <a href="/wiki/Pavement_management" title="Pavement management">pavement management</a> techniques to continually monitor road conditions and schedule <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preventive_maintenance" title="Preventive maintenance">preventive maintenance</a> treatments as needed to prolong the lifespan of their roads. Technically advanced agencies monitor the road network surface condition with sophisticated equipment such as laser/inertial <a href="/wiki/Profilometer" title="Profilometer">Profilometers</a>. These measurements include road <a href="/wiki/Curvature" title="Curvature">curvature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross_slope" title="Cross slope">cross slope</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asperity_(material_science)" title="Asperity (material science)">asperity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surface_roughness" title="Surface roughness">roughness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rut_(roads)" title="Rut (roads)">rutting</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texture_(roads)" title="Texture (roads)">texture</a>. Software algorithms use this data to recommend maintenance or new construction.
</p><p>Maintenance treatments for asphalt concrete generally include thin asphalt overlays, crack sealing, surface rejuvenating, fog sealingfo, <a href="/wiki/Pavement_milling" title="Pavement milling">micro milling</a> or <a href="/wiki/Diamond_grinding_of_pavement" title="Diamond grinding of pavement">diamond grinding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chipseal" title="Chipseal">surface treatments</a>. Thin surfacing preserves, protects and improves the functional condition of the road while reducing the need for routing maintenance, leading to extended service life without increasing structural capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thin_Surfacing_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thin_Surfacing-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Older concrete pavements that develop faults can be repaired with a <a href="/wiki/Dowel_bar_retrofit" title="Dowel bar retrofit">dowel bar retrofit</a>, in which slots are cut in the pavement at each joint, and dowel bars are placed in the slots, which are then filled with concrete patching material. This can extend the life of the concrete pavement for 15 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Failure to maintain roads properly can create significant costs to society, in a 2009 report released by the American Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials (US) about 50% of the roads in the US are in bad condition with urban areas worse. The report estimates that urban drivers pay an average of $746/year on vehicle repairs while the average US motorist pays about $335/year. In contrast, the average motorist pays about $171/year in road maintenance taxes (based on 600 gallons/year and $0.285/gallon tax).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slab_stabilization">Slab stabilization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Slab stabilization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Distress and serviceability loss on concrete roads can be caused by loss of support due to voids beneath the concrete pavement slabs. The voids usually occur near cracks or joints due to surface water <a href="/wiki/Infiltration_(hydrology)" title="Infiltration (hydrology)">infiltration</a>. The most common causes of voids are pumping, consolidation, subgrade failure and bridge approach failure. Slab stabilization is a non-destructive method of solving this problem and is usually employed with other Concrete Pavement Restoration (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concrete_Pavement_Restoration" title="Concrete Pavement Restoration">CPR</a>) methods including patching and diamond grinding. The technique restores support to concrete slabs by filing small voids that develop underneath the concrete slab at joints, cracks or the pavement edge.
</p><p>The process consists of pumping a cementitious <a href="/wiki/Grout" title="Grout">grout</a> or <a href="/wiki/Polyurethane" title="Polyurethane">polyurethane</a> mixture through holes drilled through the slab. The grout can fill small voids beneath the slab and/or sub-base. The grout also displaces free water and helps keep water from saturating and weakening support under the joints and slab edge after stabilization is complete. The three steps for this method after finding the voids are locating and drilling holes, grout injection and post-testing the stabilized slabs.
</p><p>Slab stabilization does not correct depressions, increase the design structural capacity, stop erosion or eliminate faulting. It does, however, restore the slab support, therefore, decreasing deflections under the load. Stabilization should only be performed at joints and cracks where the loss of support exists. Visual inspection is the simplest manner to find voids. Signs that repair is needed are transverse joint faulting, corner breaks and shoulder drop off and lines at or near joints and cracks. Deflection testing is another common procedure utilized to locate voids. It is recommended to do this testing at night as during cooler temperatures, joints open, aggregate interlock diminishes and load deflections are at their highest.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Testing">Testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ground penetrating <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> pulses electromagnetic waves into the pavement and measures and graphically displays the reflected signal. This can reveal voids and other defects.
</p><p>The epoxy/core test, detects voids by visual and mechanical methods. It consists of drilling a 25 to 50 millimeter hole through the pavement into the sub-base with a dry-bit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roto-hammer" title="Roto-hammer">roto-hammer</a>. Next, a two-part <a href="/wiki/Epoxy" title="Epoxy">epoxy</a> is poured into the hole – dyed for visual clarity. Once the epoxy hardens, technicians drill through the hole. If a void is present, the epoxy will stick to the core and provide physical evidence.
</p><p>Common stabilization materials include <a href="/wiki/Pozzolan" title="Pozzolan">pozzolan</a>-cement grout and polyurethane. The requirements for slab stabilization are strength and the ability to flow into or expand to fill small voids. Colloidal mixing equipment is necessary to use the pozzolan-cement grouts. The contractor must place the grout using a positive-displacement injection pump or a non-pulsing progressive cavity pump. A drill is also necessary but it must produce a clean hole with no surface <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spalling" title="Spalling">spalling</a> or breakouts. The injection devices must include a grout packer capable of sealing the hole. The injection device must also have a return hose or a fast-control reverse switch, in case workers detect slab movement on the uplift gauge. The uplift beam helps to monitor the slab deflection and has to have sensitive dial gauges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-igga_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-igga-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_sealing">Joint sealing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Joint sealing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Also called joint and crack repair, this method's purpose is to minimize infiltration of surface water and incompressible material into the joint system. Joint sealants are also used to reduce dowel bar corrosion in Concrete Pavement Restoration <a href="/wiki/International_Grooving_%26_Grinding_Association" title="International Grooving &amp; Grinding Association">(CPR)</a> techniques. Successful resealing consists of old sealant removal, shaping and cleaning the reservoir, installing the backer rod and installing the sealant. Sawing, manual removal, plowing and cutting are methods used to remove the old sealant. Saws are used to shape the reservoir. When cleaning the reservoir, no dust, <a href="/wiki/Dirt" title="Dirt">dirt</a> or traces of old sealant should remain. Thus, it is recommended to water wash, sand-blast and then air blow to remove any sand, dirt or dust. The backer rod installation requires a double-wheeled, steel roller to insert the rod to the desired depth. After inserting the backer rod, the sealant is placed into the joint. There are various materials to choose for this method including hot pour bituminous liquid, silicone and preformed compression seals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-igga_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-igga-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_considerations">Safety considerations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Safety considerations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg/220px-Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg/330px-Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg/440px-Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wavy_lines_before_pedestrian_crossing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_crossing" title="Pedestrian crossing">Pedestrian crossing</a>, line markings and <a href="/wiki/Street_furniture" title="Street furniture">street furniture</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Road_traffic_safety" title="Road traffic safety">Road traffic safety</a></div>
<p>Careful design and construction of roads can increase <a href="/wiki/Road_traffic_safety" title="Road traffic safety">road traffic safety</a> and reduce the harm (deaths, injuries, and property damage) on the highway system from traffic collisions.
</p><p>On neighborhood roads <a href="/wiki/Traffic_calming" title="Traffic calming">traffic calming</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safety_barriers" title="Safety barriers">safety barriers</a>, pedestrian crossings and cycle lanes can help protect pedestrians, cyclists, and drivers.
</p><p>Lane markers in some countries and states are marked with <a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_eye_(road)" title="Cat's eye (road)">Cat's eyes</a> or Botts dots, (bright reflectors that do not fade like paint). Botts dots are not used where it is icy in the winter, because frost and snowplows can break the glue that holds them to the road, although they can be embedded in short, shallow trenches carved in the roadway, as is done in the mountainous regions of California.
</p><p>For major roads risk can be reduced by providing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limited_access_road" title="Limited access road">limited access</a> from properties and local roads, <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade separated junctions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">median dividers</a> between opposite-direction traffic to reduce the likelihood of head-on collisions.
</p><p>The placement of energy attenuation devices (e.g. guardrails, wide grassy areas, sand barrels) is also common. Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road_fixtures" title="Road fixtures">road fixtures</a> such as road signs and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fire_hydrants" title="Fire hydrants">fire hydrants</a> are designed to collapse on impact. Light poles are designed to break at the base rather than violently stop a car that hits them. Highway authorities may also remove larger trees from the immediate vicinity of the road. During heavy rains, if the elevation of the road surface isn't higher than the surrounding landscape, it may result in flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speed_limits" title="Speed limits">Speed limits</a> can improve road traffic safety and reduce the number of <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_motor_vehicle_collisions" title="Epidemiology of motor vehicle collisions">road traffic casualties</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traffic_collisions" title="Traffic collisions">traffic collisions</a>. In their <i>World report on road traffic injury prevention</i> report, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization (WHO)</a> identify speed control as one of various interventions likely to contribute to a reduction in road casualties.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_conditions">Road conditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Road conditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Snowy_road_in_Tieringen,_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Snowy_road_in_Tieringen%2C_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg/220px-Snowy_road_in_Tieringen%2C_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Snowy_road_in_Tieringen%2C_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg/330px-Snowy_road_in_Tieringen%2C_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Snowy_road_in_Tieringen%2C_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg/440px-Snowy_road_in_Tieringen%2C_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Snowy_road_in_Tieringen,_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">Snow</a> causing bad road conditions</div></div></div>
<p><b>Road conditions</b> are the collection of factors describing the ease of driving on a particular stretch of road, or on the roads of a particular locality, including the quality of the <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">pavement surface</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pothole" title="Pothole">potholes</a>, road markings, and <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a>. It has been reported that "[p]roblems of transportation participants and road conditions are the main factors that lead to road traffic accidents".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> It has further been specifically noted that "weather conditions and road conditions are interlinked as weather conditions affect the road conditions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Specific aspects of road conditions can be of particular importance for particular purposes. For example, for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_vehicles" title="Autonomous vehicles">autonomous vehicles</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Self-driving_car" title="Self-driving car">self-driving cars</a>, significant road conditions can include "shadowing and lighting changes, road surface texture changes, and road markings consisting of circular reflectors, dashed lines, and solid lines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various government agencies and private entities, including local news services, track and report on road conditions to the public so that drivers going through a particular area can be aware of hazards that may exist in that area. News agencies, in turn, rely on tips from area residents with respect to certain aspects of road conditions in their coverage area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_performance">Environmental performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environmental performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_impacts_of_roads" title="Environmental impacts of roads">Environmental impacts of roads</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg/220px-Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg/330px-Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg/440px-Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aab_Pasadena_Highway_Los_Angeles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air pollution along Pasadena Highway in Los Angeles</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="673" data-file-width="910" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg/220px-DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg/330px-DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg/440px-DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DelhiFlyover_EDITED.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">dual carriageway</a> section of <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_8_(India)" title="National Highway 8 (India)">National Highway 8</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a></div></div></div>
<p>Careful design and construction of a road can reduce any negative environmental impacts.
Water management systems can be used to reduce the effect of pollutants from roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">Rainwater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snowmelt" title="Snowmelt">snowmelt</a> running off of roads tends to pick up gasoline, <a href="/wiki/Motor_oil" title="Motor oil">motor oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">heavy metals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">trash</a> and other pollutants and result in <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>. Road runoff is a major source of <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, copper, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cadmium" title="Cadmium">cadmium</a>, lead and <a href="/wiki/Polycyclic_aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon">polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons</a> (PAHs), which are created as <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">combustion</a> byproducts of gasoline and other <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De-icing" title="De-icing">De-icing</a> chemicals and sand can run off into roadsides, contaminate <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> and pollute <a href="/wiki/Surface_water" title="Surface water">surface waters</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road_salt" title="Road salt">road salts</a> can be toxic to sensitive plants and animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Sand applied to icy roads can be ground up by traffic into fine particulates and contribute to air pollution.
</p><p>Roads are a chief source of <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">noise pollution</a>. In the early 1970s, it was recognized<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (April 2018)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> that design of roads can be conducted to influence and minimize noise generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Noise_barrier" title="Noise barrier">Noise barriers</a> can reduce noise pollution near built-up areas. Regulations can restrict the use of <a href="/wiki/Engine_braking" title="Engine braking">engine braking</a>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle_emissions" title="Motor vehicle emissions">Motor vehicle emissions</a> contribute <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_pollutant" title="Air pollutant">air pollution</a>. Concentrations of air pollutants and adverse <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory" title="Respiratory">respiratory</a> health effects are greater near the road than at some distance away from the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carbonblack_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-carbonblack-80">[80]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road_dust" title="Road dust">Road dust</a> kicked up by vehicles may trigger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allergic" title="Allergic">allergic</a> reactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In addition, on-road transportation greenhouse gas emissions are the largest single cause of climate change, scientists say.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="464" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg/220px-A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg/330px-A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg/440px-A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A22_northbound_towards_East_Grinstead_-_geograph.org.uk_-_68150.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/A22_road" title="A22 road">A22(T)</a> with <a href="/wiki/Road_surface_marking" title="Road surface marking">line markings</a> near Summer Hill, <a href="/wiki/East_Sussex" title="East Sussex">East Sussex</a>, England</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg/220px-Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg/330px-Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg/440px-Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaluga_Region_Trassa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Road with <a href="/wiki/Guard_rail" title="Guard rail">guard rails</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kaluga_Oblast" title="Kaluga Oblast">Kaluga Oblast</a>, Russia</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="765" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg/220px-L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg/330px-L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg/440px-L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L%C3%BCtzelfl%C3%BCh-Goldbach3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Road with <a href="/wiki/Traffic_sign" title="Traffic sign">traffic signs</a> in the outskirts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bern,_Switzerland" title="Bern, Switzerland">Bern, Switzerland</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG/220px-NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG/330px-NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG/440px-NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NH_73_from_Bangalore.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/National_Highway_73_(India)" title="National Highway 73 (India)">NH 73</a> going to <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:401_3x3x3x3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/401_3x3x3x3.jpg/220px-401_3x3x3x3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/401_3x3x3x3.jpg/330px-401_3x3x3x3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/401_3x3x3x3.jpg/440px-401_3x3x3x3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:401_3x3x3x3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ontario_Highway_401" title="Ontario Highway 401">Ontario Highway 401</a>, a route with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local-express_lanes" title="Local-express lanes">collector / express</a> setup</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg/220px-Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg/330px-Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg/440px-Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manila_Cavite_Expwy_Tollgate.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The wide Coastal Road in the Philippines now called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manila-Cavite_Expressway" title="Manila-Cavite Expressway">Manila-Cavite Expressway</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation">Regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg/170px-Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg/255px-Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg/340px-Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drive_on_left_in_australia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Australian drive on left sign</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Right-_and_left-hand_traffic">Right- and left-hand traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Right- and left-hand traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">Right- and left-hand traffic</a></div>
<p>Traffic flows on the right or on the left side of the road depending on the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Why_In_Britain_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Why_In_Britain-83">[83]</a></sup> In countries where traffic flows on the right, traffic signs are mostly on the right side of the road, <a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">roundabouts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traffic_circle" title="Traffic circle">traffic circles</a> go counter-clockwise/anti-clockwise, and pedestrians crossing a two-way road should watch out for traffic from the left first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rule_of_the_Road_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rule_of_the_Road-84">[84]</a></sup> In countries where traffic flows on the left, the reverse is true.
</p><p>About 33% of the world by population drive on the left, and 67% keep right. By road distances, about 28% drive on the left, and 72% on the right,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brianlucas_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-brianlucas-85">[85]</a></sup> even though originally most traffic drove on the left worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_economics" title="Transport economics">Transport economics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roadmumbaiindia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="539" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Roadmumbaiindia.jpg/170px-Roadmumbaiindia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Roadmumbaiindia.jpg/255px-Roadmumbaiindia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Roadmumbaiindia.jpg/340px-Roadmumbaiindia.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roadmumbaiindia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A city street in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mumbai,_India" title="Mumbai, India">Mumbai, India</a> with left-hand traffic</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Transport_economics" title="Transport economics">Transport economics</a> is used to understand both the relationship between the transport system and the wider economy and the complex <a href="/wiki/Network_effect" title="Network effect">network effects</a> when there are multiple paths and competing modes for both personal and freight (road/rail/air/ferry) and where <a href="/wiki/Induced_demand" title="Induced demand">induced demand</a> can result in increased on decreased transport levels when road provision is increased by building new roads or decreased (for example California State Route 480). Roads are generally built and maintained by the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> using taxation although implementation may be through <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private</a> <a href="/wiki/General_contractor" title="General contractor">contractors</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Australia_CCG_2004_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Australia_CCG_2004-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARTBA_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARTBA-88">[88]</a></sup> or occasionally using <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">road tolls</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBTTA_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBTTA-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public-private_partnerships" title="Public-private partnerships">Public-private partnerships</a> are a way for communities to address the rising cost by injecting private funds into the infrastructure. There are four main ones:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>design/build</li>
<li>design/build/operate/maintain</li>
<li>design/build/finance/operate</li>
<li>build/own/operate</li></ul>
<p>Society depends heavily on efficient roads. In the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union (EU)</a> 44% of all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_(economics)" title="Good (economics)">goods</a> are moved by trucks over roads and 85% of all people are transported by cars, buses or coaches on roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Road_Transport_(Europe)_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Road_Transport_(Europe)-91">[91]</a></sup> The term was also commonly used to refer to <a href="/wiki/Roadstead" title="Roadstead">roadsteads</a>, waterways that lent themselves to use by shipping.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_costs">Construction costs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Construction costs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the New York State Thruway Authority,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> some sample per-mile costs to construct multi-lane roads in several US northeastern states were:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Turnpike" title="Connecticut Turnpike">Connecticut Turnpike</a> – $3,449,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Turnpike" title="New Jersey Turnpike">New Jersey Turnpike</a> – $2,200,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Turnpike" title="Pennsylvania Turnpike">Pennsylvania Turnpike</a> (Delaware Extension) – $1,970,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indiana_Toll_Road" title="Indiana Toll Road">Northern Indiana Toll Road</a> – $1,790,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Garden_State_Parkway" title="Garden State Parkway">Garden State Parkway</a> – $1,720,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Turnpike" title="Massachusetts Turnpike">Massachusetts Turnpike</a> – $1,600,000 per mile</li>
<li>Thruway, New York to Pennsylvania Line – $1,547,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ohio_Turnpike" title="Ohio Turnpike">Ohio Turnpike</a> – $1,352,000 per mile</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Turnpike" title="Pennsylvania Turnpike">Pennsylvania Turnpike</a> (early construction) – $736,000 per mile</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The United States has the largest network of roads of any country with 4,050,717 miles (6,518,997 km) as of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The Republic of India has the second-largest road system globally with 4,689,842 kilometres (2,914,133 mi) of road (2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The People's Republic of China is third with 3,583,715 kilometres (2,226,817 mi) of road (2007). The Federative Republic of Brazil has the fourth-largest road system in the world with 1,751,868 kilometres (1,088,560 mi) (2002). See <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_road_network_size" title="List of countries by road network size">List of countries by road network size</a>. When looking only at <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">expressways</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Trunk_Highway_System" title="National Trunk Highway System">National Trunk Highway System</a> (NTHS) in China has a total length of 45,000 kilometres (28,000 mi) at the end of 2006, and 60,300 km at the end of 2008, second only to the United States with 90,000 kilometres (56,000 mi) in 2005. However, as of 2017, China has 130,000 km of Expressways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_connectivity">Global connectivity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Road&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Global connectivity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2497" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG/170px-Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG/255px-Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG/340px-Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hailuoto_Ice_Road_20130113_05.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Ice_road" title="Ice road">ice road</a> between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hailuoto_Island" title="Hailuoto Island">Hailuoto Island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Finland" title="Mainland Finland">Mainland Finland</a> at winter</div></div></div>
<p>Eurasia, Africa, North America, South America, and Australia each have an extensive road network that connects most cities.
The North and South American road networks are separated by the <a href="/wiki/Dari%C3%A9n_Gap" title="Darién Gap">Darién Gap</a>, the only interruption in the <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Highway" title="Pan-American Highway">Pan-American Highway</a>. Eurasia and Africa are connected by roads on the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai Peninsula</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Peninsula" title="European Peninsula">European Peninsula</a> is connected to the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Peninsula" title="Scandinavian Peninsula">Scandinavian Peninsula</a> by the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="Øresund Bridge">Øresund Bridge</a>, and both have many connections to the mainland of Eurasia, including the bridges over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> has very few roads and no continent-bridging network, though there are a few <a href="/wiki/Ice_road" title="Ice road">ice roads</a> between bases, such as the <a href="/wiki/South_Pole_Traverse" title="South Pole Traverse">South Pole Traverse</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> is the only <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> to be connected to a continental network by road (the <a href="/wiki/King_Fahd_Causeway" title="King Fahd Causeway">King Fahd Causeway</a> to Saudi Arabia).
</p><p>Even well-connected road networks are controlled by many different legal jurisdictions, and laws such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">which side of the road to drive on</a> vary accordingly.
</p><p>Many populated domestic islands are connected to the mainland by bridges. A very long example is the 113 mi (182 km) <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Highway" title="Overseas Highway">Overseas Highway</a> connecting many of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a> with the continental United States.
</p><p>Even on mainlands, some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_that_are_inaccessible_by_road" title="List of cities that are inaccessible by road">settlements have no roads</a> connecting with the primary continental network, due to natural obstacles like mountains or wetlands, or high cost compared to the population served. Unpaved roads or lack of roads are more common in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>, and these can become impassible in wet conditions. As of 2014, only 43% of rural Africans have access to an all-season road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Due to steepness, mud, snow, or fords, roads can sometimes be passable only to <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> vehicles, those with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snow_chain" title="Snow chain">snow chains</a> or <a href="/wiki/Snow_tire" title="Snow tire">snow tires</a>, or those capable of <a href="/wiki/Deep_wading" title="Deep wading">deep wading</a> or <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_vehicle" title="Amphibious vehicle">amphibious operation</a>.
</p><p>Most disconnected settlements have local road networks connecting ports, buildings, and other points of interest.
</p><p>Where demand for travel by road vehicle to a disconnected island or mainland settlement is high, <a href="/wiki/Roll-on/roll-off" title="Roll-on/roll-off">roll-on/roll-off</a> ferries are commonly available if the journey is relatively short. For long-distance trips, passengers usually travel by air and <a href="/wiki/Car_rental" title="Car rental">rent a car</a> upon arrival. If facilities are available, vehicles and cargo can also be shipped to many disconnected settlements by boat, or air transport at much greater expense. The island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> is connected to the European road network by <a href="/wiki/Eurotunnel_Shuttle" title="Eurotunnel Shuttle">Eurotunnel Shuttle</a> – an example of a <a href="/wiki/Car_shuttle_train" title="Car shuttle train">car shuttle train</a> which is a service used in other parts of Europe to travel under mountains and over wetlands.
</p><p>In polar areas, disconnected settlements are often more easily reached by <a href="/wiki/Snowmobile" title="Snowmobile">snowmobile</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dogsled" title="Dogsled">dogsled</a> in cold weather, which can produce <a href="/wiki/Sea_ice" title="Sea ice">sea ice</a> that blocks ports, and bad weather that prevents flying. For example, resupply aircraft are only flown to <a href="/wiki/Amundsen%E2%80%93Scott_South_Pole_Station" title="Amundsen–Scott South Pole Station">Amundsen–Scott South Pole Station</a> October to February, and many residents of coastal Alaska have bulk cargo shipped in only during the warmer months. Permanent darkness during the winter can also make long-distance travel more dangerous in polar areas. Continental road networks do reach into these areas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Dalton_Highway" title="Dalton Highway">Dalton Highway</a> to the North Slope of Alaska, the <a href="/wiki/R21_highway_(Russia)" title="R21 highway (Russia)">R21 highway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Murmansk" title="Murmansk">Murmansk</a> in Russia, and many roads in Scandinavia (though due to <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjords</a> water transport is sometimes faster). Large areas of Alaska, Canada, Greenland, and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> are sparsely connected. For example, all 25 communities of <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> are disconnected from each other and the main North American road network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>Road transport of people and cargo by may also be obstructed by <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">border controls</a> and travel restrictions. For example, travel from other parts of Asia to South Korea would require passage through the hostile country of North Korea. Moving between most countries in Africa and Eurasia would require passing through Egypt and Israel, which is a politically sensitive area.
</p><p>Some places are intentionally <a href="/wiki/List_of_car-free_places" title="List of car-free places">car-free</a>, and roads (if present) might be used by bicycles or pedestrians.
</p><p>Roads are under construction to many remote places, such as the villages of the <a href="/wiki/Annapurna_Circuit" title="Annapurna Circuit">Annapurna Circuit</a>, and a road was completed in 2013 to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%AAdog_County" title="Mêdog County">Mêdog County</a>. Additional <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_and_transoceanic_fixed_links" title="Intercontinental and transoceanic fixed links">intercontinental and transoceanic fixed links</a> have been proposed, including a <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait_crossing" title="Bering Strait crossing">Bering Strait crossing</a> that would connect Eurasia-Africa and North America, a <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Strait_Bridge" title="Malacca Strait Bridge">Malacca Strait Bridge</a> to the largest island of <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> from Asia, and a <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar_crossing" title="Strait of Gibraltar crossing">Strait of Gibraltar crossing</a> to connect Europe and Africa directly.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1984/27/section/142" rel="nofollow">"Road Traffic Regulation Act 1984 – 142 General interpretation of Act"</a>. <i>Legislation</i>. <q>"road" – (a) in England and Wales, means any length of highway or of any other road to which the public has access, and includes bridges over which a road passes, and (b) in Scotland, has the same meaning as in the Roads (Scotland) Act 1984</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Legislation&amp;rft.atitle=Road+Traffic+Regulation+Act+1984+%E2%80%93+142+General+interpretation+of+Act&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.legislation.gov.uk%2Fukpga%2F1984%2F27%2Fsection%2F142&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARoad"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Direct-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Direct_13-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Direct_13-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.direct.gov.uk/en/TravelAndTransport/Highwaycode/DG_069869" rel="nofollow">"The road user and the law"</a>. <q>Most of the provisions apply on all roads throughout Great Britain, although there are some exceptions.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+road+user+and+the+law&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.direct.gov.uk%2Fen%2FTravelAndTransport%2FHighwaycode%2FDG_069869&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARoad"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100403093123/http://www.hrothgar.co.uk/WebCases/hol/reports/07/44.htm" rel="nofollow">"Judgment – Director of Public Prosecutions v. Jones and Another (On Appeal from a Divisional Court of the Queen's Bench Division)"</a>. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.hrothgar.co.uk/WebCases/hol/reports/07/44.htm" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on 2010-04-03. <q>The land over which a public right of way exists is known as a highway; and although most highways have been made up into roads, and most easements of way exist over footpaths, the presence or absence of a made road has nothing to do with the distinction. There may be a highway over a footpath, while a well made road may be subject only to an easement of way, or may exist only for the landowner's benefit and be subject to no easement at all</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Judgment+%E2%80%93+Director+of+Public+Prosecutions+v.+Jones+and+Another+%28On+Appeal+from+a+Divisional+Court+of+the+Queen%27s+Bench+Division%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.hrothgar.co.uk%2FWebCases%2Fhol%2Freports%2F07%2F44.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARoad"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.4-5.co.uk/practiceareas/index.cfm?id=486" rel="nofollow">"Local government law – Highway law"</a>. <q>Historically, a highway comprehended any path in which members of the public had the right to pass and re-pass without let or hindrance. The term embraced footpaths, bridleways, driftways and so forth. The advent of the motor vehicle and its peculiar requirements has seen increasing distinctions between paths over which walkers and riders have a right of way and those ways that are predominantly used by motor vehicles. The former may be usefully termed "rights of way" (and are the subject of a separate entry in this web) and the latter may be termed "highways."</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Local+government+law+%E2%80%93+Highway+law&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.4-5.co.uk%2Fpracticeareas%2Findex.cfm%3Fid%3D486&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARoad"></span></span>
</li>
